тАШрдЖ рдзреЗрдирд╡рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдкреНрддрджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдореЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдорддреНрд░реЗрд░рд╛рд░реНрд╖рдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдВ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдореН ред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛ –тАЩрдЖ рдзреЗрдирд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░реНрдпреВрдиреИрддрдпреЛрд░реБрдкрд╛рдиреНрддреНрдпреИрдХрдкрджрд╛ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ ред рдЕрдкреЛрдирдкреНрддреНрд░реАрдпреЗ[рез] рдПрдХрдзрдирд╛рд╕реБ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрдзрд╛рдирдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рдиреАрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рдЪрдиреАрдпрд╛[реи] ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ— рдЖ рдзреЗрдирд╡рдГ рдкрдпрд╕рд╛ рддреВрд░реНрдгреНрдпрд░реНрдерд╛рдГ рд╕рдордиреНрдпрд╛ рдпрдиреНрддреНрдпреБрдк рдпрдиреНрддреНрдпрдиреНрдпрд╛рдГ ’ (рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рел. рез ) рдЗрддрд┐ ред

Jamison Brereton

43 (397)
All Gods
Atri Bhauma
17 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except ekapad─Б vir─Бj 16
Like many All God hymns, this one enumerates in individual verses divinities deserv ing praise, and the emphasis is on the ritual and the godsтАЩ presence at and participa tion in it. There is perhaps more detail about ritual performance than in many such hymns (see, e.g., vss. 1, 3тАУ7), and this focus on the ritual is observable in two other features of the hymn. On the one hand, the god Agni dominates the last part of the hymn (vss. 12тАУ15), under the name/epithet Br╠еhaspati in verse 12, unnamed but clearly identified by his characteristics in verse 13, called ─Аyu in verse 14, and finally named in verse 15ab. Such concentration on deified ritual fire in an All God hymn is somewhat surprising. Further, the middle verse of this hymn (excluding the repeated verses at the end), verse 7, is directed not toward a god but a ritual implement, the gharma pot, used in the Pravargya ritual and often the focus of priestly speculation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

All Gods This listing impulse so evident in the last two hymns (V.41-42) is less pronounced here, though a variety of gods receive praise – with Agni especially prominent, as indicated in the published introduction.: 2 Heaven and Earth, 3 V─Бyu, 5 Indra, 6 Aramati, Agni, 7 Gharma pot, 8 A┼Ыvins, 9 P┼лс╣гan and V─Бyu, 10 Maruts, 11 Sarasvat─л, 12 Brhaspati ╠е as Agni, 13 Agni?, 14 Agni?, 15 Agni, Earth.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the kine, quick-moving, doing no harm, come to us, (laden) with their sweet fluid; the wise worshipper invokes the seven vast and joy-diffusing (rivers) for the sake of ample riches.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The kine: dhenavaс╕е = rivers

Jamison Brereton

Let the milk-cows, swift to their tasks, not neglectful, come close to us here with their milk, their honey.
For great wealth, the inspired poet, the singer keeps invoking the seven lofty (cows [=rivers?]), who are joy itself.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On mah├│ r─Бy├й see comm. ad IV.31.11. Again the published translation carelessly follows GeldnerтАЩs tr., which takes the two forms together, as if they were an adjective-noun syntagm despite the difference in case. I would now take mah├бс╕е adverbially with Oldenberg

See further ad VI.1.2.

The seven lofty and joy-bringing feminine beings (bс╣Ыhat─л╠Бс╕е sapt├б тАж mayobh├║vaс╕е) in cd, the target of our invocation, are not further specified. I have supplied тАШcowsтАЩ on the basis of ab and IX.86.25, which contains sapt├б dhen├бvaс╕е, but this is by no means certain. See other suggestions in GeldnerтАЩs n. 1. The problem is that there is no reason for the cows to number exactly seven; either тАШsevenтАЩ is, as Oberlies (Rel. RV II.74) suggests, simply an indication of totality, or some more standard group of seven, like the rivers, is being referred to (either via the image of cows or directly).

Griffith

MAY the Milch-cows who hasten to their object come harmless unto us with liquid sweetness.
The Singer, lauding, calls, for ample riches, the Seven Mighty Ones who bring enjoyment.

Geldner

Die K├╝he sollen zielschnell mit ihrer Milch zu uns kommen, mit ihrer S├╝├Яigkeit uns nicht im Stich lassend. Der redekundige S├дnger ruft die sieben Hohen, Erfreulichen zu gro├Яem Reichtum.

Grassmann

Her m├╢gen zu uns unerm├╝dlich kommen mit s├╝sser Milch zum Ziel die K├╝he eilend; Viel zu erlangen ruft der S├дnger preisend die sieben grossen lustbegabten Str├╢me.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(I purpose) to approach with pious praise, and with oblations, for (the sake of) uninjured heaven and earth may the paternal (heaven), and the sweet-spoken, free-handed, maternal (earth), both enjoying renown, defens us in every battle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With lovely praise, with reverence Heaven and Earth are to be turned hitherтАФthey who are not neglectful with regard to the prize-contest. The Father, the Mother who has honeyed speech and good handsтАФlet the two glorious ones aid us in every bout.

Griffith

With reverence and fair praise will I bring hither, for sake of strength, exhaustless Earth and Heaven.
Father and Mother, sweetof speech, fairhanded, may they, far-famed, in every fight protect us.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPriests, who are preparing (the libation), first offer to V─Бyu the delightful and brilliant (Soma); and do you, divine V─Бyu, like the Hot─Б, first drink of this sweet juice, which we offer for your exhilaration.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

First drink of this sweet juice: v─Бyu’s first drinking of the Soma is repeatedly enjoined, asakс╣Ыt prapa├▒citam

Jamison Brereton

AdhvaryusтАФhaving made the honeyed (drinks), present the pure dear (soma) to V─Бyu.
Like the Hotar, drink first of this honey of ours, god; we have given it to you for your exhilaration.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The subject of the impv. in c must also be V─Бyu, because he regularly receives the first drink of soma.

Griffith

Adhvaryus, make the sweet libations ready, and bring the beautiful bright juice to Vayu.
God, as our Priest, be thou the first to drink it: we give thee of the mead to make thee joyful.

Geldner

Adhvaryu┬┤s! Ihr habt die S├╝├Яtr├дnke bereitet, setzet dem Vayu den angenehmen klaren Saft vor! Trink zuerst wie der Hotri von diesem S├╝├Яtrank, o Gott! Wir haben ihn dir zum Rausche gespendet.

Grassmann

O Diener, die die Tr├дnke ihr bereitet, den lieben, hellen bringet dar dem Vaju; Dem Priester gleich trink du zuerst vom Safte; den s├╝ssen schenkten wir, o Gott, zur Lust dir.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe ten express of the juice, (the fingers), and the two arms of the priests, which are the dexterous immolators of the Soma, take hold of the stone; the exulting, skilful-fingered (priest) milks the mountain-born juice of the sweet Soma, and that Soma (yields its) pure juice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The text has only ┼Ыukram aс╣Г┼Ыuс╕е = sa ca aс╣Гsu‘h ┼Ыukram nirmalam rasam dugdhe, and that Soma has milked the pure juice; or aс╣Г┼Ыu may be an epithet of adhvaryu, the extensively present priest, aс╣Г┼Ыur vy─Бpto adhvaryuс╕е

Jamison Brereton

The ten fingers and the two arms hitch up the stoneтАФthe two arms with good hands that are the laboring priests [/quellers] of soma.
The plant, well(-handled by) the fists, has milked out the sap of honey that dwells on the mountain, shimmering and pure.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In b the agent noun ┼Ыamit├бr- most naturally belongs with the forms of тИЪ┼Ыam referring to ritual labor. See, e.g., in the preceding hymn V.42.10 ┼Ы├бm─лс╣Г ┼Ыa┼Ыam─Бn├бsya тАЬthe (ritual) labor of the one laboring.тАЭ However, already in the A┼Ыvamedha hymn of the RV it has acquired the euphemistic meaning тАШquellerтАЩ, that is, slaughterer, of the sacrificial beast; cf. I.162.9-10, as well as the simile in V.85.1 v├н y├│ jagh─Б╠Бna ┼Ыamit├йva c├бrma тАЬwho like a butcher a hide split apart тАжтАЭ in this maс╣Зс╕Нala. I think it likely that both senses are meant here; in post-RVic ritual texts Soma is regularly presented as a sacrificial victim.

In the 2nd hemistich Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н (cf. also Oldenberg) take c and d as separate clauses, utilizing the verb duduhe for both and supplying a priest (Geldner: Adhvaryu) as subj. of c.

The reason is nom. sug├бbhastiс╕е lit. тАШhaving good fistsтАЩ, which must otherwise modify aс╣Г┼Ы├║- тАШplantтАЩ. With Renou, in the published translation I take cd as a single clause with sug├бbhastiс╕е тАж aс╣Г┼Ы├║с╕е a single NP, assuming that тАШhaving good fistsтАЩ of the soma plant means that the plant has received good handling from the fists of its preparer. (Renou, by contrast, tr.

тАЬaux beaux rameaux,тАЭ with g├бbhasti- referring metaphorically to the growth habits of the plant.) I now think my interpr. pushes the bahuvr─лhi further than it should go, so I would now emend the tr. to тАЬ(The priest,) having good fists, has milked out the sap of the honey that dwells on the mountain; the plant has milked out its own shimmering, pure (sap).тАЭ It is likely that the verb underlying p─Бda c should be active (perhaps *dudoha); when middle forms like duduhe take an object, the subject is usually a cow or cow-substitute (as here) producing milk from itself.

Griffith

Two arms-the Soma’s dexterous immo. lators-and the ten fingers set and fix the press-stone.
The stalk hath poured, fair with its spreading branches, the mead’s bright glittering juice that dwells on mountains.

Geldner

Die zehn Finger und die Arme, die die beiden handfertigen Zubereiter des Soma sind, setzen den Pre├Яstein in T├дtigkeit. Der handgeschickte Adhvaryu hat den berggewachsenen Saft des S├╝├Яtrankes gemolken; der Stengel hat die schimmernde, helle Somamilch von sich gegeben.

Grassmann

Die Arme, die sch├╢nh├дndig Soma schaffen, und die zehn Finger schirren an den Pressstein; Der sch├╢nverzweigte Stengel str├╢met schimmernd den hellen, s├╝ssen, bergentsprungnen Saft aus.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, being well plural asd with us, bring to us, by paths frequented by the gods, the divine (feminine le), Gn─Б, mighty and omnipresent, to whom oblations are offered with reverence, who is vast and cognizant of rites, to partake of the exhilaration of the sweet Soma.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Gn─Б = str─л, a woman, a wife; commonly expresses the wife of a deity; here, it is a proper name, gn─Бm = etann─Бmik─Бm devat─Бm

Jamison Brereton

Hither to us, in agreement (with her), (bring) great Devotion [/Aramati], lady goddess, on whom the oblation is bestowed with reverence,
the lofty knower of truthтАФfor the exhilarating drink of honey, bring her hither, Agni, along the paths the gods travel.

Griffith

Bring by God-traversed paths, accordant, Agni, the great Aramati, Celestial Lady,
Exalted, worshipped with our gifts and homage, who knoweth holy Law, to drink sweet Soma.

Geldner

Grassmann

Fahr her uns, Agni, gleichgesinnt, die grosse, erhab’ne Andacht, die des Werkes kundig Die Opfer nimmt, die G├╢tterfrau, mit Ehrfurcht zum Somarausch auf gottbetretnen Pfaden.

Elizarenkova

рдпрдВ рдШрд░реНрдордВ рдорд╣рд╛рд╡реАрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рдердпрдиреНрддреЛ рди ред рдиреЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд░реНрдереАрдпрдГ ред рдЕрд╕реНрддреНрдпреБрдкрдорд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧрдГ ред рдЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рдкреНрд░рдердпрдиреНрддрдГ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рди рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬреЛрд╜рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрд╡рд╛рджрдпрдГ рд╡рдкрд╛рд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рди ред рд╡рдкрд╛рд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрджреНрдзрдВ рдкрд╢реБрдВ рдпрдерд╛рдЧреНрдиреМ рддрдкрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдирд╛ рддрдкрдиреНрддрдГ рдЕрдЮреНрдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдкрд┐рддреБрд░реНрди рдкреБрддреНрд░ рдЙрдкрд╕рд┐ рдкреНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдардГ рдкрд┐рддреБрд░реБрдкрд╕реНрдереЗ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрддрдордГ рдкреБрддреНрд░ рдЗрд╡ рдШрд░реНрдордГ рдорд╣рд╛рд╡реАрд░рдГ ред рдпрджреНрдШреНрд░рд╛рдореН рдЗрддреНрдпрдкрддрддреНрддрджреНрдзрд░реНрдорд╕реНрдп рдШрд░реНрдорддреНрд╡рдореН ’ ( рддреИ. рдЖ. рел. рез. рел) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╣рд┐ рд╢реНрд░реБрддрд┐рдГ ред рд╕рдГ рдЛрддрдпрдиреН рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН рдЕрдЧреНрдиреМ рдЖ рдЕрд╕рд╛рджрд┐ рдЖрд╕рд╛рджрд┐рддрдГ ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдкрд┐рддреГрдкреБрддреНрд░рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реНрдлреЛрдЯрд╛рджрд┐рд░рд╛рд╣рд┐рддреНрдпреЗрди рд╕реБрдЦрд╡рд╛рд╕рдкреНрд░рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдкрдирд╛рд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe vessel which the priests, celebrating (it), supply with butter, as if roasting a marrow-yielding animal with fire, has been plural ced, desirous of the sacrifice, upon the fire, like a son upon the lap of his father.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The vessel: gharma

Jamison Brereton

The one which the inspired poets anoint, like (the ritual grass) as they spread it, heating it with fire like (the offering of the sacrificial
animal) with its omentum:
the truth-(sing)ing gharma (drink/pot) has been set here on the fire like the dearest son on the lap of his father.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the position of this vs. in the hymn and its significance, see published introduction. If the vs. is an omphalos, it may focus attention on the mysteries of the Pravargya ritual.

The vs. is structured as a riddle, with the referent of y├бm (p─Бda a) withheld till d, with three similes and several technical references to ritual activities in between.

The first simile (p─Бda a) is oddly structured, in that one expects something to be compared to the unidentified acc. y├бm but there is no overt acc. expressed. Instead we must supply this acc., as the most likely object of the participle prath├бyantaс╕е тАШspreadingтАЩ (transitive), which, in default of the acc. obj. itself, carries the simile particle n├б. The object to be supplied is barh├нс╕е тАШritual grassтАЩ, which at every ritual is spread as a seat for the visiting gods. Generally the verb in the expression тАЬspread (barhis)тАЭ is тИЪstс╣Ы тАШstrewтАЩ, not тИЪprath, but, as Oldenberg points out, тИЪprath can also be used, generally for the intransitive sense тАЬ(barhis) spreadsтАЭ (V.5.4, X.70.4, etc.). The object of transitive тИЪprath is generally something much more prominent, like тАШearthтАЩ.

It may be that тИЪprath was used here to give a cosmic resonance, but it may also be partly ascribed to the alliteration in the vs.: prathayanto … v├нpr─Б, vap─Б╠Бvantam …

t├бpantaс╕е / pit├║r n├б putr├б up├бsi pr├бyiс╣гс╣нha(с╕е). The barhis is also sometimes anointed; cf. II.3.4 barh├нс╕е тАж ghс╣Ыt├йn─Бkt├бm. Thus, the absent barh├нс╕е is at the intersection of the two ritual verbs тАШspreadтАЩ and тАШanointтАЩ, and supplies the missing point of comparison in the simile тАЬThey anoint тАШwhich oneтАЩ (y├бm) like X.тАЭ The poet is inviting his audience to solve for two variables – the identity of the focus of the vs. expressed by the rel. prn. y├бm and the object to which it is compared, but he makes the second riddle easier by providing two verbs that could govern it. The overlap of the two produces the answer.

The next simile, in b, targets a different ritual substance to compare with the still unidentified y├бm. This time an accusative does appear on the surface, but it in the form of an associated adjective, vap─Б╠Бvantam тАШpossessing the/an omentum.тАЭ In classical ┼Ыrauta ritual the omentum (vap─Б╠Б) is the first and probably the most important part of the sacrificial animal to be dealt with; after the death of the animal, the omentum is removed and heated on two different fires, first preliminarily singed on the ┼ЪamitarтАЩs fire (NB: see vs. 4 and comm. thereon), then cooked on the ─Аhavan─лya fire (see my Hyenas, pp. 104-5). Here we can assume that what is identified as тАШpossessing an omentumтАЩ is the sacrificial animal (an identification supported by the occurrence of vap─Б╠Бvantam in ┼ЪB XIII.7.1.9), which itself is cooked on the fire. Sacrificial animals are also anointed; see IV.6.3 pa┼Ыv├│ anakti in a hymn that treats the animal sacrifice in some detail. Once again, the incompletely identified target of the simile is at the intersection of two ritual actions: тАШheatтАЩ and тАШanointтАЩ. In this case the similarly unidentified y├бm, the gharma pot, is also subject to both these actions in the Pravargya ritual.

The third simile, in p─Бda c, is the only one with all its parts, and is also the only one without a ritual reference. It is a version of a standard trope.

Griffith

As on his father’s lap the son, the darling, so on the fire is set the sacred caldron,
Which holy singers deck, as if extending and heating that which holds the fatty membrane.

Geldner

Der Gharmakessel, den die Redekundigen salben - wie das Barhis, wenn sie es ausbreiten, wie das mit der Netzhaut versehene Opferst├╝ck, wenn sie es am Feuer kochen ist regelrecht ans Feuer gesetzt wie der liebste Sohn auf den Scho├Я des Vaters.

Grassmann

Den sie betr├дufeln, wie am Feu’r die Priester den fettverseh’nen breiten und erhitzen, Der heil’ge Kessel ward gesetzt ans Feuer, wie in des Vaters Schooss der Sohn, der liebste.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдЪреНрдЫ рдЕрднрд┐рдореБрдЦрдореН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рд╣реБрд╡рдзреНрдпреИ рдЖрд╣реНрд╡рд╛рддреБрдВ рдЧреАрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпрд╛ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ рджреВрддреЛ рди рджреВрдд рдЗрд╡рд╛рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рддреЗрд╡ рдЧрдиреНрддреБ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ ред рдЧреАрд░реНрд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реНрдпрддреЗ ред рдорд╣реА рдкреВрдЬреНрдпрд╛ рдмреГрд╣рддреА рдорд╣рддреА рд╢рдВрддрдорд╛ рд╕реБрдЦрддрдорд╛ ред рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреА рдордпреЛрднреБрд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрдЦрд╕реНрдп рднрд╛рд╡рдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░реМ рд╕рд░рдерд╛ рдПрдХрд░рдереМ рд╕рдиреНрддреМ рдирд┐рдзрд┐рдВ рдирд┐рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рд╕реЛрдордореН рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдХреН рдЕрднрд┐рдореБрдЦрдВ рдпрд╛рддрдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрдореН ред рдзреБрд░рдВ рднрд╛рд░рд╡рд╛рд╣рд┐рдХрд╛рдВ рдирд╛рднрд┐рдореН рдЖрдгрд┐рд░реНрди рдХреАрд▓ рдЗрд╡ ред рдпрдерд╛ рдирд┐рд╖реНрдХреАрд▓рд╛ рдирд╛рднреА рд░рдердВ рди рдирд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╣рддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдпреБрд╡рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ рд╕реЛрдореЛ рдпрд╛рдЧрдВ рди рдирд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╣рддреАрддрд┐ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдпрд┐рддреБрдореЗрд╡рдВ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рддрдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay this adoring, earnest, and gratifying praise go like a messenger to summon the A┼Ыvins hither; come, A┼Ыvins, givers of happiness, riding in one chariot, come down to the deposited (Soma), as the bolt (is essential) to the axle of the wagon.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As the cart cannot move if the axle of the wheel is not fastened by the pin or bolt, so the offering of the Soma is without efficacy unless the A┼Ыvins be present

Jamison Brereton

Let the great, lofty, most availing hymn come like a messenger to invoke the A┼Ыvins.
(O A┼Ыvins,) joy itself, drive nearby on the same chariot; go to the
treasury (of honey) as if to the chariot-pole, like the axle-pin into the wheel-nave.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The last p─Бda is difficult, primarily because of dh├║ram. This would ordinarily be the acc. of the root noun dh├║r- тАШchariot poleтАЩ, and indeed that is how I take it. Geldner interprets it rather as an acc. infinitive (тАШfestzuhaltenтАЩ) to тИЪdhс╣Ы. But that aniс╣н root has no seс╣н forms in dhur- (unless dh├║r- тАШchariot poleтАЩ itself; so Whitney Roots, but see now standard alternative etymology in Schindler, Rt nouns, and EWA, both s.v.).

Witzel Got┼НтАЩs semantic interpr. (тАШzur SicherungтАЩ) is similar to GeldnerтАЩs, though derivationally distinct: they see it as a secondary abstract(ion) from the тАШchariot poleтАЩ word. Either of these analyses eases the interpr. of the p─Бda. But given the chariot-part vocab. in the rest of the p─Бda (─Бс╣З├н- тАШaxle-pin, pegтАЩ, n─Б╠Бbhi- тАШwheel-naveтАЩ), it seems highly unlikely that a standard word for a part of the chariot would in just this context not be so used – and cf. sudh├║r- тАШamenable to the chariot poleтАЩ a few vss. back (5c). I think dh├║ram has to be an unmarked simile, an acc. goal parallel to nidh├нm. The A┼Ыvins are asked to go to the nidh├н- as draft animals come tamely to the dh├║r-, then to enter it as the pin enters the nave.

I supply тАШhoneyтАЩ with nidh├нm on the basis of the phrase nidh├н- m├бdh┼лn─Бm used twice in A┼Ыvin hymns with sim. vocab.: I.183.4 ay├бс╣Г v─Бm bhag├│ n├нhita iy├бс╣Г g─л╠Бr, d├бsr─Бv im├й v─Бm nidh├бyo m├бdh┼лn─Бm тАЬHere is the portion deposited for you, here the hymn, o wondrous ones, and here the deposits of honey for youтАЭ / III.58.5 ├йh├б y─Бtam path├нbhir devay─Б╠Бnair, d├бsr─Бv im├й v─Бс╣Г nidh├бyo m├бdh┼лn─Бm тАЬTravel here along the paths leading to the gods. Wondrous ones, these stores of honey belong to you two.тАЭ Since ‘honey’ is thematic in the previous parts of this hymn (1b, 2c, 3a, d, 4c, 6c), supplying it here (esp. in A┼Ыvin context) is easy.

Griffith

Hither, as herald to invite the Asvins, come the great lofty song, most sweet and pleasant!
Come in one car, joy-givers! to the banquet, like the bolt binding pole and nave, come hither.

Geldner

Die gro├Яe hohe zusagendste Lobrede soll wie ein Bote zu den Asvin gehen, sie zu rufen. Heilbringend kommt auf einem Wagen heran, kommet um den Schatz festzuhalten wie der Zapfen die Nabe!

Grassmann

Das grosse, hehre, liebste Lied, es gehe als Bote hin, die Ritter einzuladen; Erquickend kommt zum Mahl auf gleichem Wagen, gleichwie der Zapfen in die feste Nabe.

Elizarenkova

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI offer adoration to the powerful and rapid P┼лс╣гaс╣З, and to (the powerful and rapid) V─Бyu, who are both instrumental gators of the desire of wealth and of food, (who are both) distributors of riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I have shown forth an expression of reverence to the very strong, powerful P┼лс╣гan and to V─Бyu,
who are impellers of thoughts by reason of their bounty and
treasure-givers of the prize in their own nature.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The function of ut├б in the p─Бda-final phrase ut├б tm├бn is unclear. Klein (I.347, 349) treats it as an example of an X Y ut├б construction (suggesting several diff.

possibilities), but does not consider the positional tendency of tm├бn(─Б) or the dossier of rhetorically similar phrases. Both tm├бn and tm├бn─Б have a distinct preference for p─Бda-final position, with a word consisting of two light syllables preceding as here – frequently iva, also ├║pa, etc. As a parallel to our passage, cf. esp. IX.88.3 тАж draviс╣Зod─Б╠Бiva tm├бn. I’m inclined to think that ut├б is in fact empty here (though perhaps orig. adapted from places where it made sense) and Klein’s piecemeal attempts to make sense of the various passages misplaced. Here the ut├б was perhaps slotted in because iva was inappropriate. One can also keep in mind that -a tm├бnrecalls (and replicates metrically) ─Бtm├бn-. RenouтАЩs characterization of ut├б tm├бn as тАЬtype de clausule inertтАЭ seems close to my тАЬempty.тАЭ

Griffith

I have declared this speech of adoration to mightiest Pusan and victorious Vayu,
Who by their bounty are the hymns’ inspirers, and of themselves give power as a possession.

Geldner

Ich habe das Huldigungswort f├╝r den st├дrksten, ├╝berm├дchtigen Pusan und f├╝r Vayu bestimmt, die beide durch ihre Freigebigkeit die Gedanken anregen und die selbst die Reichtumschenker des Lohnes sind.

Grassmann

Ich hab’ den Spruch gelehrt, mit dem man betet zum starken Puschan und zum schnellen Vaju, Die durch Geschenke die Gebete sch├дrfen, und welche gern auch reiche G├╝ter spenden.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBring hither J─Бtavedas, who are invoked by us all, the Maruts, under their several names and forms; come all you Maruts, with all your protecting faculties, to the sacrifice, the paises, and the adoration of the worshipper.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Convey all the Maruts according to their (individual) names, according to their (individual) forms, o J─Бtavedas, when you are invoked.
The sacrifice, the hymns, and the lovely praise of the singerтАФall you Maruts, all come (to these) with your help.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The instr. pl.s n─Б╠Бmabhiс╕е and r┼лp├йbhiс╕е identically positioned in p─Бdas a and b seem both to refer to individuated Maruts and also to make reference to the concept later to be called n─Бmar┼лpa тАШname and formтАЩ referring to the pairing of words and things differentiating the separate entities of creation. This unusual distinguishing of individual Maruts is then countered by the insistent repetition of v├н┼Ыve тАШallтАЩ referring to them as an undifferentiated class in p─Бda d. In that p─Бda I take the first v├н┼Ыve as voc. pl. with marutaс╕е (accented because p─Бda-initial) and the 2nd as a nom. with the verb, but this grammatical separation may not be nec. if the two v├н┼Ыve-s are there to match тАШnamesтАЩ and тАШformsтАЩ respectively. Vi┼Ыve Marutaс╕е also semi-equates them with the Vi┼Ыve Dev─Бс╕е.

Griffith

Invoked by us bring hither, jatavedas the Maruts all under their names and figures.
Come to the sacrifice with aid all Maruts, all to the songs and praises of the singer!

Geldner

F├╝hr alle Marut nach ihrem Namen heran, nach ihren Gestalten, o Jatavedas, wenn du darum angerufen wirst: Zum Opfer, zu den Lobesworten und zum Lobpreis des S├дngers kommet alle, ihr Marut, alle in Gnaden!

Grassmann

Fahr alle Maruts her, o Wesenkenner, und lad’ sie ein nach Namen und Gestalten; Zu Opfer, Liedern und zum Lob des S├дngers kommt her mit H├╝lfe, o ihr Maruts alle.

Elizarenkova

рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛рдЬрдиреАрдпрд╛ рджреЗрд╡реА рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА рджрд┐рд╡рдГ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рджреНрд╡рд╛ рджреЗрд╢рд╛рддреН рдмреГрд╣рддреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рддреН рд╡рд┐рд╖рдорд╛рджреНрджреЗрд╢рд╛рджрд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдорд┐рдордВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдВ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдорд╛рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдирдВ рд╕реЗрд╡рдорд╛рдирд╛ рдШреГрддрд╛рдЪреА рдШреГрддрд╛рдЮреНрдЪрдирд╛ рдЙрджрдХрд╛рдЮреНрдЪрдирд╛ рд╡рд╛ рдЙрд╢рддреА рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдорддреНрд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд╢рдЧреНрдорд╛рдВ рд╢рдХреНрддрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рд╢реГрдгреЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рее

рдиреЛрд╕реНрдорд╛рд░реНрдХрдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдВ рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА рдпрдЬрддрд╛ рдпрдЬрдиреАрдпрд╛ рджрд┐рд╡реЛрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рджрд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ, рдмреГрд╣рддреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рджрд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рд╣рд╡рдВ рдЬреБрд╖рд╛рдгрд╛ рд╕реЗрд╡рдорд╛рдирд╛ рдШреГрддрд╛рдЪреА рдЙрджрдХрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЮреНрдЪрддреА рдЙрд╢рддреА рд╣рд╡реАрдВрд╖рд┐ рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирд╛ рдиреЛрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╢рдЧреНрдорд╛рдВ рд╢рдХреНрддрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рд╢реГрдгреЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the radiant Sarasvat─л come to the sacrifice from the heavens or the spacious firmament; may the goddess, the showerer of water, propitiated by our invocation, and desirous of our gratifying praises hear.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Hither to us from lofty heaven, from the mountain let Sarasvat─л, deserving the sacrifice, come to the sacrifice.
Let the goddess, having enjoyed our call, turning toward the ghee, listen willingly to our capable speech.

Keith

To us from the sky, from the great [1] mountain;
May Sarasvati, the worshipful, come to the sacrifice

May the goddess rejoicing in our supplication, rich in ghee, May she hearken gladly to our effectual speech.

Griffith

From high heaven may Sarasvati the Holy visit our sacrifice, and from the mountain.
Eager, propitious, may the balmy Goddess hear our effectual speech, our invocation.

Geldner

Grassmann

Zu unserm Opfer komme her vom Himmel, vom hohen Berg Sarasvati, die hehre; Die butterreiche G├╢ttin h├╢re willig, den Ruf vernehmend, unsre kr├дft’ge Rede.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдереА рдЬрдиреЛ ! рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдпрд╣ (рдпрдЬрддрд╛) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╡рд╛рдгреА (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рдХрд╛рдордирд╛ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рдмреГрд╣рддрдГ) рдорд╣рджрд╛рд╢рдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рддреН) рдореЗрдШ рд╕реЗ рдЬрд▓ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ (рдЖ, рдЧрдиреНрддреБ) рд╕рдм рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрд╡реЗ (рдШреГрддрд╛рдЪреА) рдШреГрдд рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА (рдЬреБрдЬреБрд╖рд╛рдгрд╛) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╕реЗ рд╕реЗрд╡рди рдХреА рдЧрдИ (рджреЗрд╡реА) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдЧреБрдг рдФрд░ рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░ рдХреЗ рдмреЛрдз рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдЙрд╢рддреА) рдХрд╛рдордирд╛ рдХрд░рддреА рд╣реБрдИ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдХреЛ (рд╣рд╡рдореН) рдХрд╣рдиреЗ-рд╕реБрдирдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдХреЛ рд╡рд╛ (рд╢рдЧреНрдорд╛рдореН) рд╕реБрдЦрдордпреА (рд╡рд╛рдЪрдореН) рд╡рд╛рдгреА рдХреЛ рдФрд░ рд╣рдо рд▓рд╛рдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЖ, рд╢реГрдгреЛрддреБ) рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╕реБрдиреЗ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рднреА рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдИ рдпрд╣ рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдХреГрддреНрдп рдХреЛ рд╕реБрдиреЗ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИ ред рдЙрдиреНрд╣реАрдВ рдХреЛ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рд╡рд╛рдгреА рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреА рд╣реИ, рдЬреЛ рд╕рддреНрдп рдХреА рдХрд╛рдордирд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ, рдорд╣рд╛рд╢рдп, рдкрд░реЛрдкрдХрд╛рд░рдкреНрд░рд┐рдп, рдзрд░реНрдорд┐рд╖реНрда рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдкрд░реАрдХреНрд╖рдХ рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдиреЛ ! рдпрдереЗрдпрдВ рдпрдЬрддрд╛ рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА рджрд┐рд╡реЛ рдмреГрд╣рддреЛ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рдЬреНрдЬрд▓рдорд┐рд╡рд╛рд╜рд╜рдЧрдиреНрддреБ рдШреГрддрд╛рдЪреА рдЬреБрдЬреБрд╖рд╛рдгрд╛ рджреЗрд╡реНрдпреБрд╢рддреА рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реА рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА рдиреЛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдВ рд╣рд╡рдВ рд╢рдЧреНрдорд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪрд╜рд╜рд╢реГрдгреЛрддреБ рддрдереИрд╡ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдирдкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╛ рд╕рддреАрдпрдВ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдХреГрддреНрдпрдВ рд╢реГрдгреБрдпрд╛рддреН реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖ) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН (рдмреГрд╣рддрдГ) рдорд╣рд╛рд╢рдпрд╛рдиреН (рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рддреН) рдореЗрдШрд╛рддреН (рдЖ) (рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдХреН (рдпрдЬрддрд╛) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдиреНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛ (рдЧрдиреНрддреБ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддреБ (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рдореН (рд╣рд╡рдореН) рд╡рдХреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рд╢реНрд░реЛрддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛ (рджреЗрд╡реА) рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдЧреБрдгрд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдмреЛрдзрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ (рдЬреБрдЬреБрд╖рд╛рдгрд╛) рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреН рд╕реЗрд╡рдорд╛рдирд╛ (рдШреГрддрд╛рдЪреА) рдпрд╛ рдШреГрддрдореБрджрдХрдордЮреНрдЪрддрд┐ (рд╢рдЧреНрдорд╛рдореН) рд╕реБрдЦрдордпреАрдореН (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рд╡рд╛рдЪрдореН) рд╡рд╛рдгреАрдореН [(рдЙрд╢рддреА)] рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирд╛ (рд╢реГрдгреЛрддреБ) реерезрезрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Priests) plural ce the mighty Bс╣Ыhaspati, the creator whose back is dark blue, in the chamber (of sacrifice); let us worship him who is seated in the interior of the mansion, everywhere shining, golden-hued, resplendent.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Whose back is dark blue: that is, who is enveloped in smoke, from this and other attributes specified and his presence in the sacrificial chamber, the inference is that Bс╣Ыhaspati is Agni, ity─Бdi liс╣Еgair apyagnir eva Bс╣Ыhaspatiс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Here on the seat make him sitтАФthe ritual adept, dark-backed, lofty Br╠еhaspati (as Agni).
Sitting on his womb, shining here in the house, golden-colored,
reddishтАФ(him) may we serve.714 V.44

Griffith

Set in his seat the God whose back is dusky, Brhaspati the lofty, the Disposer.
Him let us worship, set within the dwelling, the red, the golden-hued, the allresplendent.

Geldner

Den hohen Meister, mit dem dunkelfarbigen R├╝cken, den Brihaspati setzet auf seinen Sitz! Wenn er seinen Platz einnimmt und im Hause leuchtet, wollen wir den Goldfarbigen, R├╢tlichen pflegen.

Grassmann

Setzt hin den Ordner, dessen R├╝cken schwarz ist, an einen Sitz, den m├дchtigen Gebets-Herrn; Lasst ehren uns den feurigen, den lichten, goldfarbigen, der in dem Hause Platz nimmt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the sustainer of all, (Agni), the greatly radiant, the delighter, come, with all his protecting (faculties), when invoked; he who is clothed with flames and with plural nts; who is irresistible; who has horns of three colours, the showerer (of benefits), the accepter of oblations.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Horns of three colours: tridh─Бtu ┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Еgaс╕е, his flames of three colours, red, white and black (or smoke). Or, tridh─Бtu may simply connote protrusions of three elemental ores

Jamison Brereton

The enduring one belonging to lofty heaven, the bestowerтАФlet him come with all his succors when he is invokedтАФ
clothing himself in his wives, the plants, not neglectful, a bull with
tripartite horn, conferring vigor [=Agni].

Jamison Brereton Notes

In d tridh─Б╠Бtu-┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Еga- тАШhaving tripartite hornsтАЩ may refer to the three hearths, though see the tripartite cows (tridh─Б╠Бtavaс╕е тАж g─Б╠Бvaс╕е), probably of Agni, in nearby V.47.4.

Griffith

May the Sustainer, high in heaven, come hither, the Bounteous One, invoked, with all his favours,
Dweller with Dames divine, with plants, unwearied, the Steer with triple horn, the life-bestower.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe holders of the (sacrificial) ladles, the ministrant priests of the man (who instrumental tutes the rite), have repaired to the bright and most excellent plural ce of the maternal (earth); offerers of the oblations, they foster the tender infant, (Agni), with worship, as people rub (the limbs of a child to promote his) existence.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMarried pairs, worn by devout rites; jointly offer abundant sacrificial food, Agni, to you who are mighty; may each individual divinity be successfully invoked by me; let them not take us into unfavourable thought.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Jointly offer: j─Бy─Бpati agnim adadh─лy─Бt─Бm, let husband and wife worship or keep up Agni

Jamison Brereton

Lofty vigor for lofty you, Agni, do those rivalrous (priestly) pairs, who reach old age through their insight, pursue.
Let every god be easy for me to invoke. Let Mother Earth not set us in disfavor.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Both Renou and Witzel Got┼Н take p─Бda a as a separate nominal clause. This is certainly possible, and an alternative tr. of the hemistich could be тАЬto you, the lofty one, there (belongs) lofty vigor, Agni. The тАж (priestly) pairs attend upon (you).тАЭ

Griffith

Agni, great vital power is thine, the mighty: pairs waxing old in their devotion seek thee.
May every Deity be swift to listen, and Mother Earth with no ill thought regard me.

Geldner

An deine, des Hotri, hohe Kraft, o Agni, halten sich die in Andacht ergrauten Ehepaare. Jeder Gott soll f├╝r mich gut zu errufen sein. Nicht soll uns die Mutter Erde in Mi├Яgunst bringen.

Grassmann

Dir Agni weihen grosse Kraft, dem grossen, im Andachtswerk ergrauet die verbundnen; Ein jeder Gott erh├╢re recht mein Rufen; nicht geb’ uns hin der Ungunst Mutter Erde.

Elizarenkova

May we come together with the present help of the A┼Ыvins, which is joy itself and provides good guidance.
Here to us bring wealth and here heroes, you two immortals, and here all that brings good fortune.

Bring riches hither unto us, and heroes, and all felicity and joy, Immortals!

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕рдореН) (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреЛрдГ) рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрдпреЛрдГ (рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджреНрдпреЗрди (рдиреВрддрдиреЗрди) рдирд╡реАрдиреЗрди (рдордпреЛрднреБрд╡рд╛) рд╕реБрдЦрдВрднрд╛рд╡реБрдХреМ (рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рдгреАрддреА) рдзрд░реНрдореНрдпрдиреАрддрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддреМ (рдЧрдореЗрдо) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рдо (рдЖ) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рд░рдпрд┐рдореН) рдзрдирдореН (рд╡рд╣рддрдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпреЗрддрдореН (рдЖ) (рдЙрдд) рдЕрдкрд┐ (рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдиреН) рдЕрддреНрдпреБрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреН рдкреБрддреНрд░рдкреМрддреНрд░рд╛рджреАрдиреН (рдЖ) (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐) рд╕рдордЧреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ (рдЕрдореГрддрд╛) рдирд╛рд╢рд░рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ (рд╕реМрднрдЧрд╛рдирд┐) рд╢реЛрднрдиреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреН реерезренрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпреЗрд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреН рдиреВрддрдирдпрд╛рд╜рдиреВрддрдирдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдпрд╛ рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдиреН рдХреГрддреНрд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ реерезренрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рддреНрд░рд┐рдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЗ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рд╡ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХ рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдирд╡реАрди рд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЪреАрди рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреЗрдиреЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдХрд░реВрди рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рд╡рд┐рддрд╛рдд рддреЗ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛рдд. рее резрен рее
